###begin article-title 0
###xml 19 26 19 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 57 61 57 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 19 26 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Fine tuning of the E. coli NusB:NusE complex affinity to BoxA RNA is required for processive antitermination
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 28 44 23 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 224 231 209 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 279 283 264 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 299 303 279 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutL</italic>
###xml 313 317 288 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR</italic>
###xml 389 393 364 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 473 476 448 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 593 597 568 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 677 681 652 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 807 812 777 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA1</italic>
###xml 816 822 786 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusE71</italic>
###xml 832 839 802 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vivo</italic>
###xml 1150 1154 1115 1119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 0 12 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">Phage lambda</span>
###xml 28 44 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 224 231 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Phage lambda propagation in Escherichia coli host cells requires transcription antitermination on the lambda chromosome mediated by lambdaN protein and four host Nus factors, NusA, B, E (ribosomal S10) and G. Interaction of E. coli NusB:NusE heterodimer with the single stranded BoxA motif of lambdanutL or lambdanutR RNA is crucial for this reaction. Similarly, binding of NusB:NusE to a BoxA motif is essential to suppress transcription termination in the ribosomal RNA (rrn) operons. We used fluorescence anisotropy to measure the binding properties of NusB and of NusB:NusE heterodimer to BoxA-containing RNAs differing in length and sequence. Our results demonstrate that BoxA is necessary and sufficient for binding. We also studied the gain-of-function D118N NusB mutant that allows lambda growth in nusA1 or nusE71 mutants. In vivo lambda burst-size determinations, CD thermal unfolding measurements and X-ray crystallography of this as well as various other NusB D118 mutants showed the importance of size and polarity of amino acid 118 for RNA binding and other interactions. Our work suggests that the affinity of the NusB:NusE complex to BoxA RNA is precisely tuned to maximize control of transcription termination.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
INTRODUCTION
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 41 57 36 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 167 168 162 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 200 203 195 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 409 412 404 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2 B3 B4">2&#8211;4</xref>
###xml 490 493 480 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 544 548 534 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 579 583 569 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxB</italic>
###xml 596 602 586 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spacer</italic>
###xml 633 634 623 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 654 658 644 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxB</italic>
###xml 713 714 703 704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 715 716 705 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 742 746 727 731 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxB</italic>
###xml 806 807 791 792 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 808 809 793 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 836 839 821 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 859 863 844 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 960 965 933 938 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10 B11 B12 B13">10&#8211;13</xref>
###xml 1051 1052 1024 1025 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 1053 1055 1026 1028 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1056 1058 1029 1031 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 1191 1192 1154 1155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 0 12 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">Phage lambda</span>
###xml 41 57 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 477 489 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">phage lambda</span>
###xml 1112 1123 <span type="species:ncbi:10742">phage HK022</span>
Phage lambda-mediated antitermination in Escherichia coli enables RNA polymerase (RNAP) to read through early transcription termination sites on the phage chromosome (1). Antitermination is regulated via the direct interaction of N protein and the transcription elongation complex (TEC) formed by RNA, RNAP and the Nus (N utilization substance) host factors NusA, NusB, NusE (S10 ribosomal protein) and NusG (2-4). N-mediated antitermination is coupled to transcription of the phage lambda nut RNA sites, each consisting of the single stranded BoxA and the palindromic stem-loop BoxB linked by a spacer sequence to which NusA binds (5). N interacts with BoxB and converts the TEC to a termination-resistant form (6,7). Binding of lambda N to BoxB results in an indirect interaction with RNAP through NusA (8,9). NusB interacts with the nut site by binding to BoxA, an interaction that is approximately10-fold strengthened upon NusE:NusB heterodimer formation (10-13). The NusB:NusE:RNA ternary complex is proposed to associate with RNAP through NusE (1,14,15). A similar complex in which lambda N is replaced by phage HK022 Nun protein induces transcription arrest on the lambda chromosome (7).
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 120 125 120 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16 B17 B18">16&#8211;18</xref>
In addition to its involvement in transcription, NusE participates in translation as part of the 30S ribosomal subunit (16-18).
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 67 70 67 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 82 89 82 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 110 112 110 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 113 115 113 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 225 227 225 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 228 230 228 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 233 237 233 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 271 282 271 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli rrn</italic>
###xml 312 316 312 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxB</italic>
###xml 365 368 365 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 386 388 386 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 454 458 449 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 488 491 483 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 520 522 515 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 82 89 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 271 278 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
A termination-resistant TEC also assembles during transcription of rrn operons in E. coli and other bacteria (19,20). In addition to Nus factors, ribosomal proteins S4, S2, L4 and L13 participate in transcription regulation (21,22). BoxA is highly conserved in all seven E. coli rrn operons. A promoter-proximal BoxB-like element is present but is not required for rrn antitermination (23). As is the case with lambda, formation of the ternary NusB:NusE:BoxA complex is a key step during rrn processive antitermination (13).
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 30 39 30 35 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 146 148 142 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 194 196 190 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 447 449 443 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 517 526 513 518 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 535 539 527 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
The structure of the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex, in which the 22 residue ribosome-binding loop of NusE was deleted, has recently been determined (24). Analysis of this structure and other data (25) suggest that NusE is the active partner of the complex and that NusB mainly acts as a loading factor for NusE, a notion that is supported by the fact that NusE in a NusB deletion background could still support N antitermination and Nun termination (24). Although UV-crosslinking studies indicate that both NusB and NusEDeltaloop contact BoxA RNA, detailed structural information about the RNA binding of NusB and the ternary NusB:NusE:RNA complex is not currently available.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 8 17 8 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA</italic>
###xml 98 105 98 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 113 121 113 121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 130 140 130 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA5</italic>
###xml 149 151 149 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 154 165 154 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA16</italic>
###xml 174 176 174 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 179 188 179 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA</italic>
###xml 197 199 197 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 238 249 238 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA69</italic>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 443 445 443 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
Several nutR BoxA mutants abolish N-mediated antitermination or Nun-mediated transcription arrest in vivo and/or in vitro, namely nutR BoxA5 (G35U) (26), nutR BoxA16 (C38A) (27), nutR BoxA (U39G) (28). Oddly, the 9-bp transversion mutant nutR BoxA69 has little effect on N-mediated antitermination except to make it NusB-independent, and it was proposed that NusB competed for BoxA binding with an as yet unidentified inhibitor of N activity (14).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 168 170 162 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 171 173 165 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 180 185 174 179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 212 215 206 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 227 235 216 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 237 239 226 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 259 264 248 253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 295 299 284 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 352 354 341 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
NusB101 (D118N) presents an intriguing gain of function variant that suppresses a block in N-mediated antitermination by NusA1 (L183R) and NusE71 (A86D) at 42degreesC (29,30). NusBD118N has enhanced affinity for rrn and lambda nut BoxA (29); for example, NusBD118N:NusE can be UV-crosslinked to BoxA-containing RNAs more efficiently than wt NusB:NusE (24). However, whether the increased affinity originates from a charge effect, from different direct contacts of the amino acid at position 118 to the RNA, or from a combination of effects is not clear.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 99 102 99 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
In the present study, we used biophysical and genetic approaches to delineate identity elements of nut RNA that are recognized by NusB and by heterodimeric NusB:NusE complex. Furthermore, we studied NusB D118 mutants to clarify the role of this amino acid in NusB:RNA and NusB:NusE:RNA interactions.
###end p 9
###begin title 10
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 10
###begin title 11
Cloning, expression and protein purification of Nus-factors
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusB</italic>
###xml 25 28 25 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 71 78 71 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 133 149 133 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 329 332 319 322 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 467 468 448 449 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sc>
###xml 71 78 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 133 161 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">Escherichia coli strain BL21</span>
The nusB gene was cloned via BamH1 and Nde1 restriction sites into the E. coli expression vector pET29b (Novagen, Madison, WI, USA). Escherichia coli strain BL21(DE3) (Novagen, Madison, WI, USA) harboring the recombinant plasmid was grown at 37degreesC in LB (Luria-Bertani) medium containing kanamycin (30 microg/ml) until an OD600 = 0.5 was reached, then the temperature was reduced to 20degreesC for 30 min and the cells were induced by 1 mM isopropyl 1-thio-beta-d-galactopyranoside (IPTG). Cells were harvested 4 h after induction, resuspended in four times the pellet weight of lysis buffer (50 mM Tris, 150 mM NaCl, 1 mM DTT, pH 7.5), and lysed by using a micro-fluidizer (Microfluidics, Newton, MA, USA). After centrifugation the supernatant was dialyzed for 4 h against lysis buffer without NaCl and afterwards applied to a HeparinFF column (GE Healthcare, Munich, Germany) using a step gradient with increasing NaCl concentrations (0-1 M). For further purification the eluted fractions containing NusB were pooled and concentrated with Vivaspin concentrators (Vivascience, MWCO 5000 Da). The concentrated sample was applied to an S75 gel filtration column (GE Healthcare). The fractions containing NusB were pooled and dialyzed against buffer as used for fluorescence measurements (25 mM HEPES, 100 mM potassium acetate, pH 7.5). The identity and structural integrity of the purified protein was analyzed by 19% SDS-PAGE and NMR spectroscopy.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
NusB mutations
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 8 13 8 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 29 34 29 34 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118R</sup>
###xml 40 45 40 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118A</sup>
###xml 51 56 51 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118E</sup>
###xml 65 70 65 70 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118K</sup>
###xml 273 276 273 276 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K2E</sup>
###xml 327 329 327 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
For NusBD118N (NusB101), NusBD118R, NusBD118A, NusBD118E and NusBD118K the mutation primers shown in  were used. Mutations were introduced by using the QuikChange protocol (Stratagene, La Jolla, CA, USA). Expression and purification was as described for wildtype NusB. NusBK2E was inherent in the original NusB pETM11-plasmid (24).
###end p 14
###begin title 15
NusE:NusB complex
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 16 19 16 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 63 70 63 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 114 116 114 116 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 243 259 243 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 407 410 397 400 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 1027 1030 1011 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 63 70 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 243 271 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">Escherichia coli strain BL21</span>
NusE was cloned via BamH1 and EcoR1 restriction sites into the E. coli expression vector pGEX-6P (GE Healthcare) (24). The recombinant plasmid encoded a GST-NusE fusion protein with an internal PreScission cleavage site following the GST-tag. Escherichia coli strain BL21(DE3) (Novagen) harboring the recombinant plasmid was grown at 37degreesC in LB medium containing ampicillin (100 microg/ml) until an OD600 = 0.5 was reached, then the temperature was reduced to 20degreesC for 30 min and the cells were induced by 1 mM IPTG. After induction overnight, the cells were harvested and resuspended in four times the pellet weight of lysis buffer (50 mM Tris, 150 mM NaCl, 1 mM DTT, pH 7.5). At this point, the NusB cell extract solved in the same buffer was added. After mixing for 20 min the cells were lysed with a micro-fluidizer (Microfluidics, Newton, MA, USA), and additional mixing was performed for 1 h to ensure correct formation of the NusB:NusE dimer. After centrifugation the dimer was purified from the supernatant via a GSTrap-FF column (GE Healthcare) using a one step elution (lysis buffer with 15 mM reduced gluthathione). The GST-NusE fusion protein was cleaved by PreScission protease while dialyzing against lysis buffer at 4degreesC overnight. The cleaved protein was reapplied to a GSTrap-FF column using the same step elution procedure, but this time collecting the flow-through. For further purification the eluted fractions containing NusB:NusE were pooled and concentrated with Vivaspin concentrators (Vivascience, MWCO 5000 Da). The concentrated sample was applied to an S75 gel filtration column (GE Healthcare). The fractions containing NusB:NusE were pooled and dialyzed against buffer as used for fluorescence measurements (25 mM HEPES, 100 mM potassium acetate, pH 7.5). The identity and structural integrity of the purified protein complexes were analyzed by 19% SDS-PAGE.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
###xml 4 9 4 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118E</sup>
###xml 14 23 14 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
NusBD118E-NusEDeltaloop production and purification for crystallization
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 43 52 43 48 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 73 75 69 71 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 287 294 283 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 378 380 374 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 437 440 433 436 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 685 690 657 662 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 695 704 667 672 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 795 804 763 768 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 814 816 778 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 287 294 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Cloning of the genes encoding NusB and NusEDeltaloop has been described (24). Mutations were introduced by using the QuikChange protocol (Stratagene, La Jolla, CA, USA). To produce protein for crystallographic analysis, plasmids containing the genes of interest were co-transformed into E. coli strain BL21(DE3) by electroporation. The cells were grown in auto-inducing medium (31) in the presence of the appropriate antibiotics to an OD600 of 0.5 at 37degreesC, and then incubated for an additional 16 h at 20degreesC. After harvesting at 4degreesC, the cell pellets were washed with binding buffer (50 mM Tris, pH 7.5, 150 mM NaCl) and stored at -80degreesC. Purification of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex followed a double affinity chromatography procedure as described for the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex (24).
###end p 18
###begin title 19
Crystallographic analysis
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 4 9 4 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 14 23 14 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 45 54 41 46 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 97 100 83 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 507 509 493 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex (NusB101:NusEDeltaloop; 16 mg/ml) was crystallized at 20degreesC via the sitting drop vapor diffusion method by mixing 1 ml of sample with 1 ml of reservoir solution (0.2 M potassium citrate, 20% PEG 3350). Crystals could be flash frozen in liquid nitrogen after transfer into 60% reservoir plus 40% glycerol. Diffraction data were collected at 100 K on beamline PXII (SLS, Villigen, Switzerland) using a MarCCD 225 mm detector. The data were processed with the XDS package (32).
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 25 30 25 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 35 44 35 40 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 127 136 123 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 160 162 152 154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 209 211 201 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 289 291 281 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
The structure of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex was solved by molecular replacement using the coordinates of the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex [PDB ID 3D3B; (24)]. The model was manually rebuilt using COOT (33) and refined by standard methodology using Refmac5 including TLS refinement (34). Each protein molecule in the crystallographic asymmetric unit represented a separate TLS group.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vivo</italic>
In vivo assays
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 0 14 0 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusB::Cam nusA</italic>
###xml 14 15 14 15 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 19 34 19 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusB::Cam nusA1</italic>
###xml 58 63 53 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cI857</italic>
nusB::Cam nusA+ or nusB::Cam nusA1 mutants carrying lambdacI857 prophage were constructed. Wild-type and mutant NusB were supplied from a pBAD30 plasmid. Phage burst size after thermal induction was determined according to standard protocols.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Fluorescence equilibrium measurements
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 43 46 43 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 86 95 81 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnG BoxA</italic>
###xml 103 110 98 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 103 110 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Various RNA sequences corresponding to the nut regions of the lambda genome or to the rrnG BoxA of the E. coli genome () were used. Fluorescence equilibrium titrations were performed using an L-format Jobin-Yvon Horiba Fluoromax fluorimeter (Edison, NJ, USA). Extrinsic fluorescence measurements with 3'-6-carboxy-fluorescein (6-FAM)-labeled RNA were performed in fluorescence buffer as above in a total volume of 1 ml using a 10 x 4 mm quartz cuvette (Hellma, Mullheim, Germany). The excitation wavelength was 492 nm, and the emission intensity was measured at 516 nm applying a 500 nm cutoff filter. Anisotropic measurements were performed with slit widths of 4 nm and 3 nm for excitation and emission, respectively. All titration measurements were carried out at 25degreesC with 50 nM of 6-FAM-labeled RNA. Following sample equilibration, six data points with an integration time of 0.8 s were collected for each titration point.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
Data fitting
###end title 26
###begin p 27

Anisotropic data were fitted to a two-state binding model to determine the equilibrium dissociation constant (Kd) using standard software. The anisotropy was calculated from:  where A, Acomplex, ARNA are anisotropies and fcomplex, fRNA are fractional intensities. The change in fluorescence intensity has to be taken into account, so that the bound fraction is given by  with A, anisotropy; ARNA, initial free anisotropy; Acomplex, anisotropy of the protein-RNA complex; P0, RNA0, total protein and RNA concentration, respectively; R, ratio of intensities of bound and free forms.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
CD measurements
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 673 674 662 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 699 700 688 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</italic>
###xml 715 716 704 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
Far UV CD measurements were performed on a J-810 S spectropolarimeter with a CDF-426S temperature control unit (JASCO International, Tokyo, Japan). Samples were prepared by dialyzing protein solutions against 10 mM sodium phosphate buffer, pH 7.5. Spectra were recorded at 25degreesC in a wavelength range of 185-260 nm with 50 nm/min scanning speed in a 1 mm path length quartz cuvette (Hellma, Mullheim, Germany) at a protein concentration of 10 muM. Buffer spectra were subtracted and ten spectra were accumulated. In order to normalize the measured ellipticity the mean residue molar ellipticity was calculated as:  Theta, measured ellipticity; MRW, mean residue mass; c, protein concentration; d, path length; N, number of amino acids.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 332 333 313 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">y</italic>

###xml 520 521 497 498 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</sub>

###xml 527 529 504 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 663 664 636 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</italic>
###xml 664 665 637 638 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 842 843 811 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 843 844 812 813 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</sub>
###xml 950 951 919 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1037 1038 1002 1003 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</italic>
###xml 1038 1039 1003 1004 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sub>
###xml 1090 1091 1055 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</italic>
###xml 1091 1092 1056 1057 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">M</sub>
###xml 1163 1164 1128 1129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">y</italic>
###xml 1164 1167 1129 1132 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">obs</sub>
###xml 1238 1239 1203 1204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="disp-formula" rid="M7">7</xref>
###xml 1244 1245 1209 1210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="disp-formula" rid="M9">9</xref>
###xml 1252 1253 1213 1214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</italic>
###xml 1253 1254 1214 1215 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 1274 1276 1235 1237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 1277 1279 1238 1240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
Thermal stability was analyzed by monitoring the CD signal at 222 nm during heating from 25degreesC to 90degreesC with a heating rate of 1degreesC/min. Quartz cuvettes with 1 cm path length equipped with a stirrer were used at a protein concentration of 2.5 muM. Both baselines and the transition region were fitted simultaneously: yobs, observed ellipticity; yn, ydy-intercepts of the baselines of native and denatured protein; mn, md, baseline slopes. DeltaHm is the enthalpy at the temperature of the melting point (TM) (35,36). Evaluations were based on the assumption that the unfolding transition is a two-state reaction. The temperature dependence of DeltaGD (free energy of unfolding) can be predicted at any temperature from the modified Gibbs-Helmholtz equation:  Over the narrow temperature range of the transition effects of DeltaCP (change in heat capacity) are negligible. Therefore, the equilibrium constant of the unfolding reaction, K, is defined as  where T is the temperature in Kelvin, R is the gas constant and DeltaSm is the entropy of unfolding at the melting point (TM). When observing a two-state process with an experimental observable, yobs, the equilibrium constant for the reaction is  By combining equations 7 and 9, DeltaGD can be calculated (36,37).
###end p 30
###begin title 31
RESULTS
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 141 149 141 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Tables 1</xref>
###xml 154 155 154 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">2</xref>

###xml 228 228 228 228 <th xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rowspan="1" colspan="1"/>

###begin title 39
Formation of the dimeric NusB:NusE complex enhances RNA binding affinity

###xml 1807 1807 1770 1770 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp736f1"/>
###xml 1158 1807 1126 1770 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F1" position="float"><label>Figure 1.</label><caption><p textid="41">Fluorescence anisotropy titration of fluorescein labeled &#955; <italic>nut</italic> and <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs with NusB (open markers) and NusB:NusE complex (filled markers). (<bold>B</bold>) Fifty nanomolar <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> (triangles) titrated with NusB. (<bold>C</bold>) A 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> (triangles) titrated with NusB/NusE. NusB bound rrnG BoxA-spacer and rrnG BoxA with nearly identical efficiencies (dissociation constants Kd of 130 +/- 20 nM and 200 +/- 10 nM, respectively; Figure 1A, Table 1). The efficiency of NusB binding to lambda nutR BoxA-spacer, nutL BoxA-spacer and nutR BoxA sequences was significantly lower (Kd values of approximately1.5 muM; Figure 1B). The higher anisotropy of nutR BoxA relative to the other constructs reflects the different rotational correlation time relative to the large RNA constructs. Preformed NusB:NusE heterodimer bound to all RNAs tested with affinities more than an order of magnitude greater than NusB alone, consistent with the findings that both NusB and NusE in the NusB:NusE complex make RNA contacts (24). Kd values for the rrnG BoxA-spacer and the rrnG BoxA were 8 +/- 2 and 5 +/- 1 nM, respectively (Figure 1A; Table 2), and 90 +/- 37 nM for nutR BoxA-spacer, 80 +/- 22 nM for nutL BoxA-spacer, and 83 +/- 8 nM for nutR BoxA (Figure 1C; Table 2). These data also indicate that contacts of NusE to the spacer region previously seen by UV-induced crosslinking (24) do not significantly increase the RNA affinity of the complex. Figure 1.Fluorescence anisotropy titration of fluorescein labeled lambda nut and rrnG RNAs with NusB (open markers) and NusB:NusE complex (filled markers). (A) A 50 nM rrnG BoxA-spacer (squares) and 50 nM rrnG BoxA (circles) titrated with NusB and NusB:NusE. (B) Fifty nanomolar nutR BoxA-spacer (circles), nutL BoxA-spacer (squares) and nutR BoxA (triangles) titrated with NusB. (C) A 50 nM nutR BoxA-spacer (circles), nutL BoxA-spacer (squares) and nutR BoxA (triangles) titrated with NusB/NusE. (D) A 50 nM nutR spacer (circles) and 50 nM nutL spacer (squares) titrated with NusB and NusB/NusE. Solid lines represent the best fit to equation (3).
###end p 40

###begin title 42
Protein RNA interaction takes place predominantly via BoxA
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 44 59 39 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA-spacer</italic>
###xml 64 73 59 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA</italic>
###xml 185 186 180 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 260 266 255 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spacer</italic>
###xml 315 326 310 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutL spacer</italic>
###xml 331 342 326 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR spacer</italic>
###xml 390 398 385 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 477 488 472 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR spacer</italic>
###xml 544 545 539 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 545 546 540 541 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
The binding of NusB and NusB:NusE to lambda nut BoxA-spacer and nutR BoxA sequences with virtually identical affinities suggests that the spacer regions, shown previously to bind NusA (5), do not bind NusB or NusB:NusE. To confirm this, we measured binding to spacer alone. Specific binding of NusB or NusB:NusE to nutL spacer and nutR spacer was not observable in fluorescence titrations (Figure 1D). A slight increase of the fluorescence anisotropy signal with the NusB:NusE nutR spacer titration is consistent with unspecific binding with a Kd-value in the upper micromolar range.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>

###xml 325 333 320 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Tables 1</xref>

###xml 613 621 608 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 630 638 625 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Tables 1</xref>
###xml 643 644 638 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">2</xref>
###xml 651 661 646 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA5</italic>
###xml 713 714 708 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 714 715 709 710 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>

###xml 905 916 888 899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA16</italic>

###xml 1052 1061 1023 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA</italic>
###xml 1365 1369 1324 1328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 1465 1469 1424 1428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 1481 1490 1440 1449 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 2.</label>
###xml 1521 1529 1475 1483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 1549 1550 1503 1504 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 1564 1565 1518 1519 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 1636 1653 1590 1607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA5-spacer</italic>
###xml 1688 1706 1642 1660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA16-spacer</italic>
###xml 1740 1758 1694 1712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic>
###xml 1781 1803 1735 1757 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA(U39G)-spacer</italic>
###xml 1881 1882 1835 1836 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 1889 1907 1843 1861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic>
###xml 1490 1974 1449 1928 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="46">Fluorescence anisotropy, &#955;<italic>nut BoxA</italic> variants and NusB (<bold>A</bold>), NusB:NusE (<bold>B</bold>). Each titration was performed with 50 nM of fluorescein labeled RNA. <italic>nutR BoxA5-spacer</italic> (filled circle, fit: solid line), <italic>nutR BoxA16-spacer</italic> (open square, fit: dashed line), <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> (filled triangle) and <italic>nutR BoxA(U39G)-spacer</italic> (open triangle, fit: dotted line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>). For <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> no interaction was observable, therefore no fitting was performed.</p>
###xml 1490 1974 1449 1928 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="46">Fluorescence anisotropy, &#955;<italic>nut BoxA</italic> variants and NusB (<bold>A</bold>), NusB:NusE (<bold>B</bold>). Each titration was performed with 50 nM of fluorescein labeled RNA. <italic>nutR BoxA5-spacer</italic> (filled circle, fit: solid line), <italic>nutR BoxA16-spacer</italic> (open square, fit: dashed line), <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> (filled triangle) and <italic>nutR BoxA(U39G)-spacer</italic> (open triangle, fit: dotted line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>). For <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> no interaction was observable, therefore no fitting was performed.</p></caption>
###xml 1974 1974 1928 1928 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp736f2"/>
###xml 1481 1974 1440 1928 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F2" position="float"><label>Figure 2.</label><caption><p textid="46">Fluorescence anisotropy, &#955;<italic>nut BoxA</italic> variants and NusB (<bold>A</bold>), NusB:NusE (<bold>B</bold>). Each titration was performed with 50 nM of fluorescein labeled RNA. <italic>nutR BoxA5-spacer</italic> (filled circle, fit: solid line), <italic>nutR BoxA16-spacer</italic> (open square, fit: dashed line), <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> (filled triangle) and <italic>nutR BoxA(U39G)-spacer</italic> (open triangle, fit: dotted line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>). For <italic>nutR BoxA69-spacer</italic> no interaction was observable, therefore no fitting was performed.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp736f2"/></fig>
Several BoxA mutations () affect lambda N antitermination and HK022 Nun transcription arrest (14,26-28). We studied the effect of these mutations on NusB and NusB:NusE binding affinities. No interaction with the boxA transversion mutant nutR BoxA69-spacer and either NusB or NusB:E heterodimer was detected (Figure 2A and B; Tables 1 and 2), clearly indicating that the binding of these factors is BoxA RNA sequence-dependent. This result supports the in vivo finding of Patterson et al. (14) that N antitermination on BoxA69 fusions is NusB-independent. We next tested BoxA point mutants that inhibit N and Nun (Figure 2A and B; Tables 1 and 2). The nutR BoxA5 mutation (G35U) reduced NusB binding 2- to 3-fold (Kd = 3.1 +/- 1.6 microM). Interestingly, the affinity of NusB:NusE heterodimer for the mutant RNA was essentially identical to that of NusB (Kd = 5.2 +/- 1.3 microM). NusB and NusB:NusE bound nutR BoxA16 (C38A) with Kd values of 5.1 +/- 1.4 microM and 3.4 +/- 1.8 microM, respectively. The dissociation constants of NusB and NusB:NusE for nutR BoxA (U39G), which inhibits N, were 1.6 +/- 0.8 microM and 1.9 +/- 0.7 microM, respectively. Judged from their effects on the NusB and NusB:NusE binding affinities, G35 and C38 participate more tightly in protein binding than U39. The equivalent binding affinities of NusB and NusB:NusE heterodimer to these BoxA point mutants stands in sharp contrast to the enhanced binding of the heterodimer to wild-type BoxA sequences. Figure 2.Fluorescence anisotropy, lambdanut BoxA variants and NusB (A), NusB:NusE (B). Each titration was performed with 50 nM of fluorescein labeled RNA. nutR BoxA5-spacer (filled circle, fit: solid line), nutR BoxA16-spacer (open square, fit: dashed line), nutR BoxA69-spacer (filled triangle) and nutR BoxA(U39G)-spacer (open triangle, fit: dotted line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (3). For nutR BoxA69-spacer no interaction was observable, therefore no fitting was performed.
###end p 45

###xml 1793 2703 1710 2615 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="50">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein-labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> and <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs towards NusB<sup>D118N</sup> (<bold>A</bold> and <bold>B</bold>) and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE complex (<bold>C</bold> and <bold>D</bold>) (filled markers) compared to the wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE complex (open markers, data as in <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>A and C). (A) Fifty nanomolar <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB; (B) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> alone (triangles) titrated with Nus<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB. (C) A 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE; (D) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> (triangles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE. Dashed lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>) for NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>/NusE, respectively. Solid lines the similar fit for wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE.</p>
###xml 1793 2703 1710 2615 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="50">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein-labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> and <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs towards NusB<sup>D118N</sup> (<bold>A</bold> and <bold>B</bold>) and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE complex (<bold>C</bold> and <bold>D</bold>) (filled markers) compared to the wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE complex (open markers, data as in <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>A and C). (A) Fifty nanomolar <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB; (B) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> alone (triangles) titrated with Nus<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB. (C) A 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE; (D) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> (triangles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE. Dashed lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>) for NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>/NusE, respectively. Solid lines the similar fit for wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE.</p></caption>
###xml 2703 2703 2615 2615 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp736f3"/>
###xml 1784 2703 1701 2615 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F3" position="float"><label>Figure 3.</label><caption><p textid="50">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein-labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> and <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs towards NusB<sup>D118N</sup> (<bold>A</bold> and <bold>B</bold>) and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE complex (<bold>C</bold> and <bold>D</bold>) (filled markers) compared to the wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE complex (open markers, data as in <xref ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>A and C). (A) Fifty nanomolar <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB; (B) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> alone (triangles) titrated with Nus<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB. (C) A 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA</italic> (circles) titrated NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE; (D) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic> (circles), <italic>nutL BoxA-spacer</italic> (squares) and <italic>nutR BoxA</italic> (triangles) titrated with NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE and NusB:NusE. Dashed lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>) for NusB<sup>D118N</sup> and NusB<sup>D118N</sup>/NusE, respectively. Solid lines the similar fit for wild-type NusB and NusB:NusE.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp736f3"/></fig>
NusBD118N is a gain- of-function mutation that enables NusB to override mutations in NusE and NusA that abrogate lambda N-mediated antitermination (29,30). The dissociation constants for NusBD118N complexes with rrnG BoxA-spacer and rrnG BoxA were 5- to 6-fold lower compared to wild-type NusB (Figure 3A; Table 3). Only small reductions in Kd were observed for the nutL BoxA-spacer and nutR BoxA-spacer complexes, whereas the dissociation constant for the complex of NusBD118N with nutR BoxA decreased significantly from approximately1600 nM to approximately290 nM (Figure 3B; Table 1). In contrast, the mutation increased the Kd values about 3-fold for heterodimer complexes with rrnG BoxA-spacer and rrnG BoxA (Figure 3C, Table 2). NusBD118N:NusE complexes with nutR BoxA-spacer and nutL BoxA-spacer sequences displayed 3- and 5-fold, respectively, lower Kd values for the mutant relative to the wild-type heterodimer (Figure 3D, Table 3). For the NusBD118N:NusE complex with nutR BoxA, the Kd decreased by nearly an order of magnitude to 9 +/- 1 nM (Figure 3D; Table 2). Thus, NusE did not further enhance the binding of NusBD118N to rrnG BoxA or rrnG BoxA-spacer. However, NusE strongly stimulated the binding of NusBD118N to sequences derived from nutL and nutR. (A) Fifty nanomolar rrnG BoxA-spacer (squares) and 50 nM rrnG BoxA (circles) titrated with NusBD118N and NusB; (B) 50 nM nutR BoxA-spacer (circles), nutL BoxA-spacer (squares) and nutR BoxA alone (triangles) titrated with NusD118N and NusB. (<bold>A</bold>) Ribbon plot of the <italic>E. coli</italic> NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE<sup>&#916;loop</sup> complex. NusB<sup>D118N</sup>, green; NusE<sup>&#916;loop</sup>, orange. Residues at position 118 are shown as sticks and a magnified view of the residue 118 region is provided (carbon, as the respective molecule; oxygen, red; nitrogen, blue). The orientation relative to (A) is indicated. (<bold>D</bold>) Comparison of the electrostatic surface potentials of the complexes. Blue, positive charge; red, negative charge. Left, NusB<sup>D118N</sup>:NusE<sup>&#916;loop</sup> complex. Right, NusB:NusE<sup>&#916;loop</sup> complex. The positions of residue 118 are circled. The orientations are the same as in (B).</p>

###xml 1446 1453 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
NusEDeltaloop is a derivative of NusE that binds NusB and retains transcriptional but not translational activity (24). The NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex binds RNA that includes a BoxA sequence, although with lower efficiency than NusB:NusE [(24); ; Table 2]. Previous studies demonstrated that NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop bound RNA more tightly than NusB:NusEDeltaloop. To ask if the increased RNA affinity of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex correlated with structural rearrangements compared to the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex, we solved the crystal structure of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex by molecular replacement at 2.5 A resolution (Figure 4). The structure was refined to Rwork and Rfree factors of 20.4% and 25.6%, respectively (Table 4). An asymmetric unit of the crystal contained three molecules each of NusBD118N and NusEDeltaloop, which formed three NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complexes. Two of these complexes exhibited well-defined electron density, but the electron density map of the third complex was fragmentary: In that complex, residues 60-77 and 127-139 of NusBD118N and residues 45-47 and 60-72 of NusEDeltaloop could not be unambiguously traced. The following discussion therefore refers to the structures of the two well defined complexes, which closely resemble each other [RMSD of 0.75 A for 220 Calpha atoms; calculated with SSM (38)]. Figure 4.Structure of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex. (A) Ribbon plot of the E. coli NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex. NusBD118N, green; NusEDeltaloop, orange. Secondary structure elements and termini are labeled. The orange sphere marks the site at which the ribosome-binding loop of NusE has been replaced by a single serine. (B) Comparison of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex (left) with the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex [right, PDB ID 3D3B; (24)]. Insets: closeup views of the residue 118 regions. The orientation relative to (A) is indicated. Gray mesh, final 2Fo - Fc electron density of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop structure contoured at the 1sigma level and covering N118 and neighboring residues. The orientation relative to (A) is indicated. (C) Superimposition of the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex [blue and red, PDB ID 3D3B; (24)] and of NusB [grey, PDB ID 1EY1; (39)] on the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex (green and orange). Residues at position 118 are shown as sticks and a magnified view of the residue 118 region is provided (carbon, as the respective molecule; oxygen, red; nitrogen, blue). The orientation relative to (A) is indicated. (D) Comparison of the electrostatic surface potentials of the complexes. Blue, positive charge; red, negative charge. Left, NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex. Right, NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex. The positions of residue 118 are circled. ###begin p 56
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</sup>

###begin p 60
###xml 28 33 28 33 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 54 63 54 59 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 134 136 130 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 176 184 168 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 225 230 217 222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 235 244 227 232 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 300 309 288 293 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 356 364 336 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 712 721 692 697 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 805 813 777 785 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 947 955 919 927 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1043 1048 1015 1020 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 1073 1082 1045 1050 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
The global structure of NusBD118N in complex with NusEDeltaloop is very similar to that of wild-type NusB in isolation [PDB ID 1EY1; (39); rmsd of 2.54 A for 110 Calpha atoms; Figure 4]. Furthermore, the structure of the NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex is virtually identical to that of the NusB:NusEDeltaloop complex (RMSD of 0.85 A for 220 Calpha atoms; Figure 4B), demonstrating that the D118N mutation has no global conformational consequences. In particular, the positions and conformations of NusB residue N118 in the mutant and of residue D118 in the parent complex are essentially identical. Irrespective of the amino acid at position 118, the neighboring region undergoes identical adjustments upon NusEDeltaloop binding, during which the Calpha position of residue 118 is repositioned by 2.8 A (Figure 4C, inset). However, the D118N exchange induces a significant difference in the local electrostatic surface properties of the complex (Figure 4D). This observation is consistent with the idea that the increased RNA affinity of NusBD118N or its complex with NusEDeltaloop is at least in part due to the replacement of a negatively charged residue with an uncharged residue at the RNA binding site, thus reducing repulsion with the negatively charged sugar-phosphate backbone of the RNA. Alternatively, or in addition, introduction of an asparagine for an aspartate at position 118 may result in additional hydrogen bonds to the RNA.
###end p 60
###begin title 61
The overall structures of various NusB118 mutants are highly similar
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 308 316 304 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 685 686 677 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</italic>
###xml 686 687 678 679 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 783 788 771 776 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118K</sup>
###xml 843 848 831 836 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>

###xml 1070 1072 1058 1060 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>

###xml 1344 1347 1324 1327 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRW</sub>
###xml 1375 1376 1355 1356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 1380 1381 1360 1361 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 1503 1508 1483 1488 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>

###xml 1252 1595 1240 1575 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="63">(<bold>A</bold>) Overlay of the CD-spectra for the NusB variants. &#920;<sub>MRW</sub> versus wavelength in nm. &#920;<sub>MRW</sub> was according to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>). ###xml 1595 1595 1575 1575 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp736f5"/>
###xml 1243 1595 1231 1575 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F5" position="float"><label>Figure 5.</label><caption><p textid="63">(<bold>A</bold>) Overlay of the CD-spectra for the NusB variants. &#920;<sub>MRW</sub> versus wavelength in nm. &#920;<sub>MRW</sub> was according to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>). (<bold>B</bold>) Thermal unfolding for the NusB variants. Fraction of the unfolded species versus absolute temperature. NusB (blue), NusB<sup>D118N</sup> (green), NusB<sup>D118A</sup> (black), NusB<sup>D118R</sup>, (red), NusB<sup>D118E</sup> (orange) and NusB<sup>D118K</sup> (grey).</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp736f5"/></fig>
###xml 245 254 <span type="species:ncbi:45245|species:ncbi:137466|species:ncbi:475014|species:ncbi:319979">e. minima</span>
To investigate further the effect of amino acid variations at position 118, several point mutations with positively charged, negatively charged, and apolar amino acids were examined. All NusB variants show CD-spectra typical of alpha-helices, i.e. minima at 208 nm and 222 nm as well as a maximum at 190 nm (Figure 5A), with only minor differences from the wild-type protein spectrum. The melting temperatures of NusB and NusB D118 variants were determined by thermal unfolding. The CD signal at 222 nm, which we used to indicate melting, was reduced by all mutations, particularly by substitutions with positively charged residues. The Gibbs free energy of the unfolded species (DeltaGD) at 328 K thus ranges from 8.3 +/- 0.2 kJ/mol for wild-type NusB to 1.6 +/- 0.2 kJ/mol for NusBD118K. The NusB variants, with the notable exception of NusBD118N, show very similar unfolding transitions. The broader transition of NusBD118N indicates a lower value for the Gibbs free energy of the unfolding reaction at 328 K and for the free reaction enthalpy at the melting point [(35,36); Figure 5 and Table 3]. These relatively small differences indicate that the D118 point mutations do not lead to global NusB misfolding or to unstable NusB proteins. Figure 5.(A) Overlay of the CD-spectra for the NusB variants. ThetaMRW versus wavelength in nm. ThetaMRW was according to equation (4). (B) Thermal unfolding for the NusB variants. Fraction of the unfolded species versus absolute temperature. NusB (blue), NusBD118N (green), NusBD118A (black), NusBD118R, (red), NusBD118E (orange) and NusBD118K (grey).
###end p 62

###xml 1318 1327 1306 1315 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 6.</label>
###xml 1395 1398 1378 1381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>

###xml 1746 1762 1729 1745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA-spacer</italic>
###xml 1327 1763 1315 1746 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="66">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> or <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs and NusB<sup>D118A</sup> (open circle, fit: bold line), NusB<sup>D118R</sup> (filled square, fit: dashed line), NusB<sup>D118E</sup> (open triangle, fit: pointed line) and NusB<sup>D118K</sup> (filled triangle, fit: dashed/pointed line). ###xml 1327 1763 1315 1746 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="66">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> or <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs and NusB<sup>D118A</sup> (open circle, fit: bold line), NusB<sup>D118R</sup> (filled square, fit: dashed line), NusB<sup>D118E</sup> (open triangle, fit: pointed line) and NusB<sup>D118K</sup> (filled triangle, fit: dashed/pointed line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>). (<bold>A</bold>) Fifty nanomolar <italic>rrnG BoxA;</italic> (B) 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer;</italic> (<bold>C</bold>) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA</italic>; and (<bold>D</bold>) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic>.</p></caption>
###xml 1763 1763 1746 1746 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp736f6"/>
###xml 1318 1763 1306 1746 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F6" position="float"><label>Figure 6.</label><caption><p textid="66">Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein labeled &#955;<italic>nut</italic> or <italic>rrnG</italic> RNAs and NusB<sup>D118A</sup> (open circle, fit: bold line), NusB<sup>D118R</sup> (filled square, fit: dashed line), NusB<sup>D118E</sup> (open triangle, fit: pointed line) and NusB<sup>D118K</sup> (filled triangle, fit: dashed/pointed line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>). (<bold>A</bold>) Fifty nanomolar <italic>rrnG BoxA;</italic> (B) 50 nM <italic>rrnG BoxA-spacer;</italic> (<bold>C</bold>) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA</italic>; and (<bold>D</bold>) 50 nM <italic>nutR BoxA-spacer</italic>.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp736f6"/></fig>
The binding properties of different NusB mutants dependent on the RNA were tested. Thus the binding of NusBD118A to rrnG BoxA-spacer was approximately as tight as NusB+, whereas the affinity of the mutant for rrnG BoxA was 20% that of NusB+ (Figure 6; Table 1). NusBD118E bound rrnG BoxA with wild-type efficiency but associated with rrnG BoxA-spacer approximately2-fold less well than NusB+. We considered the possibility that replacing D118 with a positively charged residue might enhance binding through ionic interactions with the RNA ligand. This was not the case. Neither NusBD118K nor NusBD118R bound rrnG RNA with wild-type efficiency. The higher volumes of the lysine and arginine residues may induce unfavorable steric interactions, canceling out positive contributions to binding by electrostatic interactions with RNA. Consistent with this idea is our observation that NusBD118R bound rrn or nutR BoxA less efficiently than NusBD118K, reflecting, perhaps, the larger volume of the former substitution. Of the various D118 substitutions, interaction with the nutR BoxA-spacer could be detected only for NusBD118N and NusBD118E (Figure 6 and Table 3). NusBD118E bound nutR BoxA as well as NusB+. NusBD118A and NusBD118K bound nutR BoxA significantly better than wild-type NusB (Figure 6 and Tables 1 and 2). Figure 6.Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein labeled lambdanut or rrnG RNAs and NusBD118A (open circle, fit: bold line), NusBD118R (filled square, fit: dashed line), NusBD118E (open triangle, fit: pointed line) and NusBD118K (filled triangle, fit: dashed/pointed line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (3). (A) Fifty nanomolar rrnG BoxA; (B) 50 nM rrnG BoxA-spacer; (C) 50 nM nutR BoxA; and (D) 50 nM nutR BoxA-spacer.
###end p 65

With the exception of NusBD118E, NusE significantly enhanced mutant NusB binding to rrnG RNA, although no mutant except NusBD118N bound as well as NusB+:NusE. NusE also enhanced binding to nutR sequences. Binding of NusB mutants to nutR BoxA was, except for NusBD118E, at least as strong as NusB+. Thus, NusE may foster additional RNA contacts, rendering NusB-mediated interactions less dominant (Figure 7 and Tables 1 and 2). ###xml 440 456 435 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutR BoxA-spacer</italic>
Fluorescence anisotropy measurements with fluorescein labeled lambdanut and rrnG RNAs to NusBD118A:NusE (open circle, fit: solid line), NusBD118R:NusE (filled square, fit: dashed line), NusBD118E:NusE (open triangle, fit: pointed line) and NusBD118K:NusE (filled triangle, fit: dashed/pointed line). Lines represent the best fit to equation (3). (A) Fifty nanomolar rrnG BoxA; (B) 50 nM rrnG BoxA-spacer; (C) 50 nM nutR BoxA; and (D) 50 nM nutR BoxA-spacer.
###end p 69

###xml 1496 2023 1455 1943 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="73">NusB is carried on pBAD30 and induced with 0.2% arabinose. Cells were grown overnight at 32&#176;C in LB + ampicillin (50 &#181;g/ml), diluted 1:100 into the same medium + 0.2% arabinose, and grown at 32&#176;C for 1 h. &#955; was induced by temperature shift to 42&#176;C for 90 min. Burst size was determined by plating the lysate on W3110 at 37&#176;C. Cells were titered at 32&#176;C prior to temperature shift; titers were equivalent for all strains. Values represent an average of two experiments; variation was &lt;8 %.</p>
###xml 1496 2023 1455 1943 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF10"><p textid="73">NusB is carried on pBAD30 and induced with 0.2% arabinose. Burst size was determined by plating the lysate on W3110 at 37&#176;C. Cells were titered at 32&#176;C prior to temperature shift; titers were equivalent for all strains. Values represent an average of two experiments; variation was &lt;8 %.</p></fn>
###xml 1496 2023 1455 1943 <table-wrap-foot xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><fn id="TF10"><p textid="73">NusB is carried on pBAD30 and induced with 0.2% arabinose. Values represent an average of two experiments; variation was &lt;8 %.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot>
###xml 1307 2023 1271 1943 <table-wrap xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="T5" position="float"><label>Table 5.</label><caption><p textid="72">Strains are W3110 <italic>nusB::Cam</italic> &#955;<italic>cI857</italic> lysogens</p></caption><table frame="hsides" rules="groups"><thead align="left"><tr><th rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>nusB</italic> plasmid</th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>nusA<sup>+</sup></italic></th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>nusA1</italic></th><th rowspan="1" colspan="1">Suppression (%)</th></tr></thead><tbody align="left"><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">&#8722;</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">103</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.0004</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">&lt;0.01</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">+</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">137</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">&lt;0.01</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">D118N</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">85</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">4.2</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">4.9</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">D118A</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">74</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.4</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.5</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">D118E</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">44</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">0.005</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">&lt;0.01</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">D118K</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">113</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2.5</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">2.2</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">D118R</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">125</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">4.2</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">3.3</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><fn id="TF10"><p textid="73">NusB is carried on pBAD30 and induced with 0.2% arabinose. ###xml 94 106 <span type="species:ncbi:10710">phage lambda</span>
We next tested the NusB D118 mutants for suppression of nusA1 (nusAL183R). nusAL183R prevents phage lambda growth at 42degreesC by blocking lambda N antitermination. Over-expression of NusB D118 mutants in a nusA+ lambda cI857 lysogen had modest negative effects on phage burst size (Table 5). The negatively charged NusBD118E was most inhibitory, reducing burst size to 32% of wild-type levels. In the nusAL183R background, all mutants except NusBD118E increased burst size >100-fold. NusBD118N suppressed nusAL183R with greatest efficiency, increasing burst size from <0.0l% to 4.9% relative to nusA+. NusBD118K and NusBD118R also significantly enhanced lambda growth (to 2.2% and 3.3%, respectively, of nusA+ titers). Suppression by NusBD118A was the least effective (0.5%). Taken together, these data suggest that replacing the negatively charged asp118 with an uncharged asparagine residue or a positively charged lysine or arginine residue significantly restores lambda N activity in a nusAL183R strain. Poor suppression by the alanine substitution may reflect the lower molecular weight of this aminoacid relative to aspartate. Similarly, the inability of NusBD118E to restore lambda growth may also be caused by steric effects due to the bulky glutamate side chain, in spite of its negative charge. Cells were grown overnight at 32degreesC in LB + ampicillin (50 microg/ml), diluted 1:100 into the same medium + 0.2% arabinose, and grown at 32degreesC for 1 h. lambda was induced by temperature shift to 42degreesC for 90 min. Burst size was determined by plating the lysate on W3110 at 37degreesC. Cells were titered at 32degreesC prior to temperature shift; titers were equivalent for all strains. Values represent an average of two experiments; variation was <8 %.
###end p 71
