###begin title 74
DISCUSSION
###end title 74
###begin p 75
###xml 147 150 147 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 271 274 271 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2 B3 B4">2&#8211;4</xref>
###xml 299 302 294 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 382 389 372 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn nut</italic>
###xml 457 459 447 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 460 462 450 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 977 985 967 975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
Processive transcription antitermination depends on formation of a multi-factorial ribonucleoprotein complex on the surface of RNAP in response to nut signaling sequences in the untranslated leader regions of transcripts. These factors include NusA, NusB, NusE and NusG (2-4). In the case of lambda nut, lambda N protein forms part of the complex, whereas the complex that forms at rrn nut includes the Nus proteins and a number of additional host factors (21,22). Protein-protein and protein-RNA interactions in these complexes are cooperative in the sense that a stable complex is assembled based on numerous, but often weak, binary interactions. While some of these binary interactions have been mapped within the complexes, little is known about their relative strengths and how important these are for generating functional complexes. Here, we have used a combination of biophysical and functional studies to explore interactions between NusB or NusB:NusE complex and the nut BoxA RNA signaling sequence to which it binds.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 108 110 108 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 221 229 216 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 320 328 305 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 328 329 313 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 383 387 368 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 454 458 439 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 519 521 504 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
We confirm that the affinity of NusB:NusE for BoxA is an order of magnitude higher than that of NusB alone (13), reflecting, presumably, the additional contacts that NusE makes with BoxA. We find that mutations in lambda nut BoxA that inhibit lambda N antitermination reduce NusB binding. However, in contrast to lambda nut BoxA+, the affinities of NusB and NusB:NusE for the mutant BoxA sequences are essentially identical. The mutations lie throughout BoxA and do not define the known sites of NusE-RNA interactions (24).
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 4 5 4 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 5 6 5 6 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 82 90 77 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 191 193 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 249 265 244 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrnG BoxA-spacer</italic>
###xml 298 299 293 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 299 300 294 295 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 503 509 498 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 663 671 658 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn BoxA</italic>
###xml 676 684 671 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 773 774 768 769 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 774 775 769 770 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 882 883 877 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 883 884 878 879 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 897 912 892 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn BoxA-spacer</italic>
###xml 960 961 955 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 961 962 956 957 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 982 998 977 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nutL BoxA-spacer</italic>
The Kd values reported above for the association of NusB or NusB:NusE with lambda nut BoxA are similar to those reported by Greive and coworkers based on fluorescence anisotropy experiments (13). We note, however, a large difference with respect to rrnG BoxA-spacer binding. These authors report a Kd of 850 nM for NusB and 200 nM for NusB:NusE, whereas we observe values of 130 nM and 8 nM, respectively. Since the RNA sequences tested were identical, we suggest that the lower affinity seen by Greive et al. reflects the 5' location of the fluorescent label on their RNA compared to the 3' location used in our experiments. The N-terminus of NusB contacts both rrn BoxA and nut BoxA at their 5'-ends, and interference with these contacts by a 5' label could increase the Kd values, although in an RNA sequence-dependent manner. Indeed, we find that the K2E mutation increased the Kd of the NusB rrn BoxA-spacer complex from 130 nM to 3600 nM, but raised the Kd of NusB binding to nutL BoxA-spacer only 2-fold (from 2200 nM to 5100 nM).
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 47 52 47 52 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 77 82 77 82 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 169 171 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 172 174 167 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 238 243 233 238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 248 251 243 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 272 273 267 268 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 354 356 349 351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 358 360 353 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 430 438 425 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn BoxA</italic>
###xml 450 459 440 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA.</italic>
###xml 499 507 484 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 517 522 502 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA5</italic>
###xml 527 537 512 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA(U39G)</italic>
###xml 571 577 556 562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA16</italic>
###xml 681 685 661 665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 703 710 683 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 748 756 728 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 821 826 801 806 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 836 844 816 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn BoxA</italic>
###xml 869 870 849 850 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1042 1045 1017 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
We have also explored the phenotype of the NusBD118N (NusB101) mutation. NusBD118N suppresses mutations in NusA and NusE that inhibit lambda N antitermination function (29,30). It has been proposed that an increase in the affinity of NusBD118N for nut RNA compared to NusB+ may compensate for weaker RNA (or protein) contacts of the mutant Nus proteins (24, 29). We show here that the D118N mutation enhances NusB binding to both rrn BoxA and lambda nut BoxA. The mutation reduces binding to lambda nut BoxA mutants, BoxA5 and BoxA(U39G), but has no effect on binding to BoxA16. It will be interesting to test whether the D118N mutation further reduces lambda N antitermination on BoxA mutant templates in vivo. D118N also enhances NusB binding to nut BoxA in complex with NusE. However, we find that the affinity of NusBD118N:NusE for rrn BoxA is only 20% that of NusB+:NusE. These data imply that D118N, although it optimizes the formation of the lambda N antermination complex, interferes with the assembly of antitermination complexes on rrn operons.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 29 34 29 34 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 38 42 38 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 136 141 136 141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118N</sup>
###xml 146 155 146 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 194 195 190 191 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 200 209 196 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
###xml 280 288 272 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 328 336 320 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
The enhanced affinity of NusBD118N to BoxA is not due to gross distortions in the shape of the NusE complex. Thus, the structure of NusBD118N:NusEDeltaloop complex is virtually identical to NusB+:NusEDeltaloop, although the electrostatic surface properties are strongly affected (Figure 4D). In fact, CD spectroscopic analyses (Figure 5) show that NusB also structurally tolerates a number of other mutations at position 118. Thus, the effects of the D118 mutations on RNA binding are local.
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 58 62 58 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 305 310 305 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA1</italic>
###xml 315 321 315 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusE71</italic>
D118 is located close to NusB residues that interact with BoxA RNA. It was suggested that removal of the negatively charged aspartate with the neutral asparagine residue might extend the NusB RNA-binding surface and that this might stabilize the antitermination complex and account for the suppression of nusA1 and nusE71. Our results in general support this notion, although we find that the size of the D118 substitution also plays a role in the affinity of NusB for RNA.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 95 102 95 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 181 186 176 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cI857</italic>
###xml 198 202 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA</italic>
###xml 202 203 197 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 208 213 203 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA1</italic>
###xml 315 320 305 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA1</italic>
###xml 445 446 430 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 474 482 459 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 584 585 569 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 585 586 570 571 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 594 595 579 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 600 608 585 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut BoxA</italic>
###xml 666 671 651 656 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D118K</sup>
###xml 738 743 718 723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nusA1</italic>
The differential RNA affinities of the mutant NusB:NusE complexes roughly correlate with their in vivo suppression activity. We measured the burst sizes after induction of a lambda cI857 lysogen in nusA+ and nusA1 hosts. This assay, which reflects the ability of lambda N to antiterminate, showed that the order of nusA1 suppression efficiency was D118N > D118R > D118K > D118A. D118E failed to increase lambda burst size over that seen for NusB+. The binding affinities to nut BoxA for the mutants in complex with NusE was D118N > D118 > D118R > D118A > D118K > D118E. Note that the Kd of NusB+ for nut BoxA (83 nM) was not significantly different from that of NusBD118K (75 nM), yet the mutant NusB increased the lambda burst size in a nusA1 host at least 100-fold above the wild-type NusB level. This disjunction between RNA binding and N activation is, as yet, unexplained. It implies, however, that D118 may make functionally important contacts within NusB or with NusE.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 38 42 38 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 394 398 394 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 470 479 470 475 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;loop</sup>
We propose that D118 does not contact BoxA, but that removal of the negative charge permits such interaction. The location of position 118 opposite the NusB:NusE interaction surface renders an effect of mutations at this position on the NusB:NusE interaction unlikely. However, it cannot be ruled out completely, and a more definitive verdict needs further structural analysis of the NusB:NusE:BoxA complex. Study of how NusB mutations affect complex formation with NusEDeltaloop and alter its RNA binding properties might shed further light on the role of the NusE loop in RNA binding.
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 366 368 366 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 431 435 431 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BoxA</italic>
###xml 459 465 459 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spacer</italic>
###xml 521 522 521 522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 582 585 582 585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 590 593 590 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrn</italic>
###xml 681 684 681 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 705 708 705 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nut</italic>
###xml 761 763 761 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
The results from our combined biophysical and genetic investigations illustrate how a particular protein-RNA interaction is fine-tuned with respect to other interactions within a functional ribonucleoprotein complex to achieve processive transcriptional antitermination. Furthermore, our results refine the mechanism by which NusB acts as a NusE RNA loading factor (24). NusB:NusE:RNA complex formation is entirely mediated by the BoxA sequences, whereas the spacer regions are necessary and sufficient for NusA binding (5). Sterically, simultaneous binding of these Nus factors to nut and rrn should be possible. There is, however, no evidence that NusA and NusB:NusE interact at nut, and no increase in nut binding by NusB:NusE was observed on NusA addition (15).
###end p 83
